## Section 001: Planning Execution Workflow Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without its two governing rules, classify work before loading process, and write plans so a zero-context engineer can execute them in reviewed batches
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because A01 opens with not all work deserves the same process, and writing-plans demands plans assuming the engineer has zero context for the codebase and questionable taste
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the doctrine splits across two layers that can be misapplied, A01 governs which process to run while the skill pair governs how a chosen plan is written and executed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference operationalizes A01's four-flow classifier and the writing-plans and executing-plans skill pair, not project-management methodology at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the classify-first rule, the four flows with their time scales, and the plan-then-batch-execute contract the skills add beneath Feature and Product work
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the two layers share one premise, process is a cost to be justified, A01 buys the lightest safe flow while the skills buy reviewer checkpoints only at batch boundaries instead of every step
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Planning Execution Workflow Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify incoming work through the decision tree, run the matched flow, and for plan-driven work write bite-sized tasks and execute them three at a time with review between batches

- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists corpus-hygiene failures while the corpus names its own, over-processing light work, under-processing unclear work, plans that say add validation instead of complete code, guessing through blockers, and starting implementation on main without consent
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each is stated with its guard, A01's classifier for process mismatch, writing-plans' complete-code rule for vague plans, and executing-plans' stop list for guessing
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the two layers' anti-patterns differ in blast radius, misclassification wastes a session while a forced-through blocker can corrupt the deliverable
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry names workflow anti-patterns with detectors and does not police code quality inside tasks
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add rows for process-weight mismatch in both directions, incomplete plan steps, blocker guessing, skipped batch reports, and main-branch implementation without consent
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the plan-side anti-patterns are all context assumptions, every writing-plans rule exists because the executor is assumed to know nothing, so the detector is asking what the executor would have to already know
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to scan plans for exact paths, complete code, and expected outputs, and scan execution logs for classification, batch reports, and stop events
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because each is stated with its guard, A01's classifier for process mismatch, writing-plans' complete-code rule for vague plans, and executing-plans' stop list for guessing
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the two layers' anti-patterns differ in blast radius, misclassification wastes a session while a forced-through blocker can corrupt the deliverable
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the registry names workflow anti-patterns with detectors and does not police code quality inside tasks
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add rows for process-weight mismatch in both directions, incomplete plan steps, blocker guessing, skipped batch reports, and main-branch implementation without consent

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names the corpus verifier while the theme's real gates are per-layer, A01's common-sense test before process loads, per-step verification commands inside plans, and batch-boundary review before execution continues
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because writing-plans requires exact commands with expected output per step, and executing-plans forbids skipping verifications and requires reporting verification output at each batch boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the gates assume plans were written to the skill's standard, improvised plans carry no runnable verification to gate on
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gate set defines what must pass before work advances between steps, batches, and flows, not the repository's own corpus verifier semantics
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt three gate layers, classification recorded before process loads, each plan step's verification run as specified, and each batch closed with a report and explicit readiness for feedback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the batch report is a gate disguised as courtesy, saying ready for feedback transfers control to the reviewer, making continuation an approval rather than a default
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to gate every plan-driven session on the three layers in order, recording verification output verbatim in batch reports
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because writing-plans requires exact commands with expected output per step, and executing-plans forbids skipping verifications and requires reporting verification output at each batch boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the gates assume plans were written to the skill's standard, improvised plans carry no runnable verification to gate on
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the gate set defines what must pass before work advances between steps, batches, and flows, not the repository's own corpus verifier semantics
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: adopt three gate layers, classification recorded before process loads, each plan step's verification run as specified, and each batch closed with a report and explicit readiness for feedback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the batch report is a gate disguised as courtesy, saying ready for feedback transfers control to the reviewer, making continuation an approval rather than a default

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide keys usage to theme mentions instead of the states that trigger it, work arriving unclassified, a spec needing a plan, or a written plan needing execution
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the two skills name their triggers exactly, writing-plans fires when you have a spec for a multi-step task before touching code, and executing-plans when you have a written plan for a separate session
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: keying to every mention of planning would drag the doctrine into trivial tasks the classifier routes to lighter flows
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes readers into this reference and does not classify their work for them
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to trigger on three states, unclassified work enters at A01's decision tree, a spec without a plan enters at writing-plans, and a plan without progress enters at executing-plans

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scenario shows a builder choosing a pattern and stops before the journey the corpus scripts, classify the work, write a zero-context plan, then execute it batch by batch with reports and stops
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus hands off explicitly, writing-plans ends by offering subagent-driven or parallel-session execution, and executing-plans picks up the saved plan file in a fresh session
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one journey cannot cover all four flows, Bug and Enhancement journeys never touch the plan-execution machinery
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scenario dramatizes one representative plan-driven journey and does not cover the lighter flows
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the journey through a Feature-flow shape, classification at the decision tree, a plan with exact paths and complete code saved to docs/plans, execution in three-task batches, one mid-batch stop at an unclear instruction, and completion through the finishing sub-skill

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic evidence agreement instead of this theme's variables, work-type certainty, scope clarity, executor context, and the cost of process mismatch in each direction
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because A01 prices the trade explicitly, over-process wastes time and under-process builds the wrong thing, and its time budgets make the stakes concrete per flow
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: classification is fallible, A01's own signal is retrospective, budgets blowing past expectations mean the classification was probably wrong
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide calibrates process weight per work item and cannot waive the verification gates inside a chosen flow
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey adopt to full plan-and-batch discipline for Feature and Product work, adapt to light PRD and TDD for Enhancement work, and avoid heavy process for Bugs where the flow is reproduce, test, fix
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the trade is asymmetric with scope uncertainty, under-processing unclear work compounds because wrong things get built on wrong things, while over-processing clear work wastes only the ceremony itself
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to when classification is uncertain between two flows, run the lighter one but watch the time budget as the tripwire

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed artifact names a lifecycle diagram while this theme's operational artifact is a plan document written to the skill's template plus its execution record of batch reports
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because writing-plans mandates the header block, goal, architecture, tech stack, and bite-sized task structure, and executing-plans emits batch reports with verification output as it runs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: plan artifacts for work the classifier routes to Bug or Enhancement flow are the over-processing A01 warns against
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the artifact certifies this reference is operational and does not grade the code the plan produced
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as one plan file in docs/plans form with header, exact paths, complete code, and expected outputs, paired with its batch reports and any stop events

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed metrics name lead time and generic signals without this theme's observables, classification-versus-budget variance, stop events per session, plan-gap discoveries mid-execution, and batch report cadence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because A01 designates budget overrun as the misclassification signal, and executing-plans' stop triggers mark exactly where plans failed their zero-context contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: stop events read as failure but are the discipline working, their absence in long sessions is the suspicious signal
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the metrics gauge workflow discipline, not the product quality of what was built
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt budget variance per flow, stop events with their trigger types, plan gaps found in execution, and batches per report as primary signals
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that plan-gap counts are the cheapest plan-quality feedback, every mid-execution stop for a missing dependency or unclear instruction names a specific writing-plans rule the plan violated
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record per session the classification, budgeted versus actual time, stop events, and plan gaps, and route gap patterns back to plan-writing practice
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because A01 designates budget overrun as the misclassification signal, and executing-plans' stop triggers mark exactly where plans failed their zero-context contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; stop events read as failure but are the discipline working, their absence in long sessions is the suspicious signal

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds endpoints per batch but not this theme's working units, work items classified per session, plan tasks written per plan, and tasks executed per batch
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus sets the numbers itself, batches default to three tasks, plan steps run two to five minutes, and A01 budgets whole flows from hours to months
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the skill's batch size is a default, not a law, and no source bounds how many tasks one plan should carry
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds the planner's and executor's work per session and does not bound the flows' calendar budgets, which A01 owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rebound the model around one plan per feature, tasks decomposed to the two-to-five-minute step grain, execution in three-task batches, and one flow's work per session
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the step grain is the load-bearing bound, two-to-five-minute steps force decisions into the plan and out of execution, which is what makes batches reviewable and stops rare

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table carries hygiene and traffic rows and omits how workflow sessions actually fail, misclassified work discovered late, plans with gaps that strand executors, blockers guessed through, and reviews skipped until errors compound
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus names each with its guard, A01's budget tripwire for misclassification, the stop triggers for plan gaps and blockers, and the batch cadence for review starvation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: misclassification surfaces latest and costs most, its first hard signal is a blown budget after real work is sunk
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table covers workflow-level failures, while documentation-process failures stay with the seed rows
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add misclassification, plan-gap stranding, blocker guessing, and review starvation rows, each with its source-named signal, blast radius, and repair
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the failures chain, a misclassified Feature gets no plan, planlessness leaves the executor guessing, and guessing without review checkpoints compounds unchecked, so the earliest guard is worth the most

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify verification failures generically and never carry this theme's retry rules, repeated verification failure is a stop trigger, not a retry loop, and blown budgets trigger reclassification, not harder pushing
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because executing-plans lists verification fails repeatedly among its stop-and-ask conditions, and A01 reads persistent budget overrun as evidence the classification is wrong
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reclassification mid-work costs the process already loaded, a Feature reclassified to Product restarts discovery on sunk PRD work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retrying workflow-level work and reference-verification runs, kept as two labeled layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the workflow-layer rules, one bounded rerun for a failed step verification then stop and ask, plan gaps route back to plan revision rather than executor improvisation, and repeated budget overruns route to reclassification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the corpus's backpressure is social, not mechanical, every hard failure routes to the human partner, ask for clarification rather than guessing, so escalation is the designed relief valve rather than the last resort
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to diagnose which layer failed before any retry, rerun a step verification once, and route persistent failures to the partner with the plan or classification change named
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because executing-plans lists verification fails repeatedly among its stop-and-ask conditions, and A01 reads persistent budget overrun as evidence the classification is wrong
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; reclassification mid-work costs the process already loaded, a Feature reclassified to Product restarts discovery on sunk PRD work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this governs retrying workflow-level work and reference-verification runs, kept as two labeled layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the workflow-layer rules, one bounded rerun for a failed step verification then stop and ask, plan gaps route back to plan revision rather than executor improvisation, and repeated budget overruns route to reclassification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the corpus's backpressure is social, not mechanical, every hard failure routes to the human partner, ask for clarification rather than guessing, so escalation is the designed relief valve rather than the last resort

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: reclassification mid-work costs the process already loaded, a Feature reclassified to Product restarts discovery on sunk PRD work
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are retrying by adding process feels rigorous but inverts A01, a failing Enhancement needs reclassification or a fixed plan, not a Product-weight ceremony

### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?

## Section 022: Observability Checklist

- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets recycle generic evidence records and never name this theme's evidence stream, the classification record, the plan file, the batch reports with verification output, and the stop events

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: full records for Bug-flow sessions are ceremony, the lighter flows warrant lighter evidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this covers observing workflow sessions, not the executed code's runtime telemetry

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method fixes handler latency numbers while this theme's performance question is A01's own table, whether Bug work lands in hours, Enhancements in days, Features in weeks, and Products in months
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because A01 publishes per-flow budgets down to the phase level, thirty minutes of PRD for an Enhancement, sixteen hours of TDD for a Feature, making the claim directly checkable against session records
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the budgets' provenance is unstated, they arrived with A01 rather than from measured local sessions, so they are calibration targets, not verified facts
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this evaluates the workflow discipline's time claims, not code performance, keeping the seed's latency defaults as the absent-SLO fallback
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure actual time per flow phase against A01's table and read persistent variance as either misclassification or a table needing local recalibration
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the budget table serves double duty, prospectively it sizes work and retrospectively it detects misclassification, but only the retrospective use has a stated rule, so measurement is what activates the table's tripwire function

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement recites multi-system limits and misses this theme's scale walls, plans too large for one executor session, work items spanning multiple flows at once, and portfolios of concurrent items competing for the same reviewer
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine assumes one work item, one flow, one plan, one executor, and one reviewing partner, and every assumption breaks separately at scale
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: scaling advice beyond the single-item shape is inference here, no source addresses concurrent items or multi-executor plans
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the boundaries bound this reference and its discipline, not team-level project management
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add scale signals, plans split across sessions at batch boundaries, items needing two flows decomposed into separate items, and reviewer saturation when batch reports queue faster than feedback returns
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the reviewer is the scaling bottleneck by design, checkpoints exist to route control through a human, so parallel plan execution multiplies report traffic into a single approval channel and quietly converts checkpoints into rubber stamps
